Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Machine Joint Association

Request to Enforce the Clothing System Regulations 126

The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Association yesterday submitted a petition to the Chairman of the National Government and the President of the Executive Yuan, as well as the Ministers of Interior, Finance, Industry, and Commerce, requesting the strict enforcement of the clothing system regulations and effective restrictions on Western attire. The petition stated that since the promulgation of the regulations, which limit the use of domestically produced robes and gowns, half a year has passed. It was hoped that in the future, the whole country would uniformly comply and implement these regulations, so that the sales of domestically produced silk, cotton, hemp, and woven products could be restored to their former glory, and the industry could rely on this to make rapid progress, giving businesses a chance to survive. However, the reality is far from this. Looking around the market, foreign goods stores are everywhere, and foreign clothing is as prevalent as ever. The domestic silk and cotton weaving industry is declining day by day. Today, the global trend is to promote domestic goods in order to alleviate unemployment and restore production. Examples include the Queen of England personally using domestic products, Japan's strict austerity policies, India's use of indigenous cloth, and Turkey's promotion of domestic goods. There are too many examples to list. Given China's extreme poverty, the whole country should unite in using domestic goods to block loopholes and cultivate the national foundation, so as to resist the economic aggression of the great powers and gradually seek strength. However, the people of the whole country compete to regard wearing foreign clothes as fashionable, and all clothing and food tends towards foreign styles. This is the root cause of financial exhaustion and national weakness. If fundamental and strict prohibitions are not enforced, and compliance with the regulations is not urged, it will be impossible to achieve the effect of changing customs and influencing behavior from above. A few days ago, our association convened an emergency meeting of silk weaving colleagues from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and all unanimously agreed to petition the government to reaffirm the clothing system regulations, effectively restrict Western attire, and issue orders to all levels of government agencies to set an example and take the lead in complying with the regulations, or else be punished for violating the law. If this can be carried out swiftly and resolutely, then the people of the whole country will be proud to wear domestic goods and regard Western attire as disrespectful. In this way, within a few years, not only will the domestic bulk industries be able to restore their original production, but unemployed workers will also be able to be accommodated as much as possible, and the national economy and the livelihood of businesses will be maintained and developed. We earnestly request your departments to take our sincere intentions into consideration and approve our proposal for implementation, so that the national economy and the people's livelihood can truly benefit from it.

Zhang Yaozeng's Views on Foreign Legal Persons 127

Mitsui vs. He Hong Case 128

The case of Mitsui & Co. v. He Hong et al. was heard for the second time at the Special District Court the day before yesterday. The plaintiff's representative, lawyer Okamoto, and the second defendant's representative, lawyer Zhang Yaozeng, engaged in a major debate on the issue of legal person status. This was reported in the previous newspaper. We interviewed lawyer Zhang to inquire about the intent of his arguments at the time. Mr. Zhang said that the newspaper's report was largely accurate, but there were some omissions, so he elaborated on his views as follows: (1) There is a major principle that must be explained first in refuting the plaintiff's claims, namely the effectiveness of the law. Statutory law is stronger than customary law, and later law prevails over earlier law. This is a theorem in jurisprudence. However, there is considerable debate as to whether laws or treaty laws (i.e., clauses in treaties relating to the rights and obligations of the people in civil matters) are superior. Some people say that treaties cannot directly take effect domestically and must be enacted into law and promulgated separately in accordance with the content of the treaty law before they can take effect domestically. This theory inevitably emphasizes the law. The prevailing view today is that a promulgated treaty has the same effect as a law. A treaty can change a law, and a law can also change a treaty. The effectiveness is still determined by the general rule that later law prevails over earlier law. Therefore, within the existing legal system of a country, the most recently enacted law has the strongest effect. When a court hears a case, it must take the most recently enacted law as the highest standard. All other old customs, old laws, and old treaties that conflict with the most recent law have no basis for assertion. This is indeed a major principle adopted in the legal system of civilized countries. Now, China's recently implemented important laws such as the Civil Code and the Enforcement Rules of the General Principles of the Civil Code are indeed the highest standard laws governing civil affairs. Their effectiveness is higher than all previous civil laws and regulations. However, the plaintiff's lawyer insisted on relying on some old treaties and old customs to resist the application of the most recent laws. Regardless of whether what he relied on was already invalid or inherently illegal, it has no value for consideration. Even if what he relied on had no flaws, according to the major principle that new law prevails over old law, it is obviously untenable. This point is the biggest mistake in the plaintiff's defense. His argument is fundamentally unacceptable precisely because of this. (2) The plaintiff claims that foreigners subject to consular jurisdiction are not subject to Chinese laws and regulations unless otherwise provided for in special treaties. Therefore, the legal person status of a foreign legal person should be determined by the law of its home country. This argument is untenable today. In the past, treaties providing for consular jurisdiction, if they conflicted with the most recent laws, according to the major principle that later law prevails over earlier law, that part of the treaty could not be asserted again in court. This is self-evident. Now, Article 11 of the Enforcement Rules of the General Principles of the Civil Code clearly stipulates that foreign legal persons are not recognized unless otherwise provided for by law. Then, regardless of what treaties existed before, if a foreign legal person claims its personality in a Chinese court, it can only apply the provisions of this Article 11. Unless there is a law or treaty that changes this article in the future, this is a definite and supreme rule. Moreover, the Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce has long expired and become invalid. The new treaty has not yet been concluded. It can be said that there is no basis for the Japanese to claim consular jurisdiction. In July 1928, the National Government promulgated Article 4 of the Provisional Measures for the Application of Old Treaties between the Republic of China and Various Foreign Countries before the New Treaties were Concluded, stating that foreigners in China should be subject to the laws of China and the jurisdiction of Chinese courts. Since the new Sino-Japanese treaty has not been concluded, it is naturally subject to its control. However, the plaintiff actually said that the National Government publicly recognized that the Japanese have consular jurisdiction, which is even more contrary to the facts. To go one step further, even when the consular jurisdiction treaties were valid in the past, their effect only extended to cases where foreigners were defendants. Cases where foreigners were plaintiffs were all handled in Chinese courts in accordance with Chinese law. Now, the foreign legal person is the plaintiff, but it invokes consular jurisdiction to say that it should not be subject to Chinese laws and regulations. Such an expansion of consular jurisdiction was unreasonable even in the past, let alone today. As for the plaintiff's citation of several cases to illustrate that Chinese courts have never denied foreign legal persons on the grounds of non-registration, it is even more untenable to say that foreign legal persons do not need to be recognized today. In the past, the Shanghai Mixed Court and the Provisional Court handled the most cases involving foreigners as plaintiffs and Chinese as defendants. It is true that the foreign legal person was not denied, but the Mixed Court was an illegal organization of foreigners after the 1911 Revolution, and the Provisional Court was clearly a temporary measure agreed upon by the local authorities and foreign consuls. It has no legitimate status in Chinese law, needless to say. Other formal courts have no clear precedents for recognizing foreign legal persons, but the Supreme Court has an explicit statement denying all foreign firms as legal persons (Supreme Court Precedent 7, Shangzi, 1158). To go one step further, even if the formal courts had tacitly recognized foreign legal persons in the past, all conflicting practices would naturally become invalid after the implementation of the Civil Code and have no basis for assertion. The plaintiff also said that the current Special District Court's hearing of cases where foreign legal persons are plaintiffs is tantamount to recognizing them as having legal personality by virtue of its authority, which is also a misunderstanding. The court can investigate the existence or lack of the parties' capacity at any time. Regardless of the stage of the litigation, if the court finds that it is lacking, it can order it to be corrected or reject the lawsuit. Therefore, the first instance's failure to discover its lack does not prevent the second and third instances from investigating and correcting it. It cannot be said that the court's acceptance of the case without immediate investigation means that it has recognized its personality. In short, regardless of whether there is consular jurisdiction or not, regardless of past practices, in cases where foreigners are now plaintiffs suing Chinese in the Shanghai Special District Court, according to Article 2 of the New Agreement of the Shanghai Public Concession Court, Chinese laws and regulations, whether substantive or procedural, must be applied uniformly now or in the future. And according to Article 11 of the current Enforcement Rules of the General Principles of the Civil Code, foreign legal persons are not recognized unless otherwise provided for by law. Therefore, Mitsui & Co. has no basis for asserting its legal person status unless it obtains recognition in accordance with Chinese law. (3) The plaintiff also said that even if foreign legal persons are subject to Chinese law, there is no need for foreign legal persons to register according to the current interpretation of the law. This is even more wrong. Article 6 of the Enforcement Rules cited by the plaintiff specifically refers to Chinese public interest legal persons and has nothing to do with foreign for-profit organizations. There is no need to discuss it in depth. Although Article 1 of the Enforcement Rules states that civil matters that occurred before the implementation of the General Principles of the Civil Code are not subject to the provisions of the General Principles of the Civil Code, it clearly states that this is limited to cases where there are no special provisions in the Enforcement Rules. Now, Articles 11 to 15 of the Enforcement Rules, all five articles, are special provisions regarding foreign legal persons. The general purport of these provisions is that foreign legal persons cannot have the same legal capacity unless they follow the same establishment procedures as Chinese legal persons. The intent is very clear. If it is said that there is no need for foreign legal persons to register under the current law, then where will these magnificent major articles be placed? (4) The plaintiff also said that China's laws are incomplete, and it is difficult for foreigners to register even if they want to. This is even more ignorant. Article 11 of the Enforcement Rules stipulates that foreign legal persons are not recognized unless they are established in accordance with the law, and Article 13 of the same article stipulates the method of recognition, that is, foreign legal persons who set up offices in China may apply mutatis mutandis the provisions of the Civil Code regarding the establishment of various legal persons. Mutatis mutandis means that foreign legal persons shall apply the provisions of the Chinese legal persons' establishment and apply them to produce the same legal results. This kind of mutatis mutandis applies to all kinds of legal persons. Now, let's just talk about companies. A company is a kind of for-profit organization. According to Article 45 of the Civil Code, which is applied mutatis mutandis, its qualifications should be determined by special law, and Article 6 of the current Company Regulations, a special law, stipulates that the establishment of a company cannot be asserted against a third party unless it is registered with the competent authority where the head office is located. Then, a foreign legal person who sets up an office in China cannot assert its legal person status against a third party, that is, against persons other than the company, unless it is registered with the competent authority where its office is located. This is very clear. However, the plaintiff said on the one hand that there are no provisions for the registration of foreign legal persons in the Company Regulations. The Enforcement Rules clearly state that mutatis mutandis shall of course be in accordance with the provisions of the Chinese legal persons. Why is there a need for separate provisions? If the Company Law has provisions for foreign legal persons, then it can be applied directly. Why must the Enforcement Rules stipulate it as mutatis mutandis? On the other hand, the plaintiff said that Mitsui & Co. has already registered at its head office in Japan, and no one can contest it. This is even more incomprehensible of the mutatis mutandis. A foreign legal person sets up an office in China, so mutatis mutandis, the provisions of the Chinese company's head office registration are applied, requiring it to register at the location of the office. This is the reason for specifying mutatis mutandis. If one sticks to its words without any changes, it is application. Moreover, if this were the case, the legal provisions for mutatis mutandis would be meaningless. Thirdly, the plaintiff said that a third party refers to a person who has no contractual relationship with the company, which is even more bizarre. Our Article 6 of the Company Regulations was originally based on Article 45 of the Japanese Company Law, and scholars of that law all explain that a third party refers to all persons other than the company's founders and the company. It has never been heard that a person who has a contract with the company is not a third party. I only know that a person who has a contract with an unregistered company can assert that the contract is invalid on the grounds of non-registration. The above are all misinterpretations by the plaintiff. The plaintiff also said that the procedures for legal person registration are incomplete and the court has no registration preparation, which is even more wrong. Article 10 of the Enforcement Rules of the General Principles stipulates that the court is the registration authority, but only for those who register in accordance with the Civil Code, that is, only for the registration of public interest legal persons. As for for-profit legal persons, the Company Registration Rules, which are mutatis mutandis, stipulate it very clearly in Article 34 of the Legal Person Registration Rules. As for registration in accordance with the Company Law, the Provisional Company Registration Rules stipulate it in great detail. It has been implemented for a long time. Foreign companies apply mutatis mutandis the Company Regulations and of course apply mutatis mutandis the Registration Rules. How can it be said that the registration provisions are lacking? In short, our current legal system treats foreign legal persons equally and gives them the same treatment as Chinese legal persons. Any foreign legal person who sets up an office in China, whether it is for public interest or for profit, whether it is a company or a foundation, must obtain the same rights and obligations as Chinese legal persons of the same type as long as they follow the same establishment procedures as Chinese legal persons of the same type. This is the inevitable conclusion based on the systematic interpretation of the Enforcement Rules of the General Principles of the Civil Code, the Company Regulations of the Civil Code, etc. Its spirit is broad and fair, and it is more than any civilized country's laws. The plaintiff uses the incompleteness of Chinese law as an excuse, but I believe that Chinese law is extremely perfect in this respect.

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Implements Austerity Measures 129

Abolishing Departments and Laying Off Employees The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, in order to reorganize its internal affairs and implement austerity policies, announced the implementation of these measures yesterday (July 1). The details are as follows:

Abolishing the Warehouse Department: The company had specially established a Warehouse Department to manage the many docks and warehouses, with Hong Yanbin as the department head. From July 1st, this department will be abolished, and the various docks and warehouses will be directly under the jurisdiction of the head office, without the need for the department head to relay. Hong Yanbin will be reassigned as the accounting director. The general manager will select diligent employees from the other department members and staff, retain seven or eight people, and send them to the various warehouse management offices in the port to assist in warehouse affairs. The rest will be laid off.

Canceling Auditors: The company originally had a department of external auditors who were sent to various ports and ships to investigate affairs. Now, because the company's budget has been established to match income and expenditure, it has no choice but to implement austerity policies. Yesterday, it issued a notice to dismiss all of the more than 20 external auditors.

Establishing an Affairs Department: When the Business Department merged with the Shanghai Bureau last month, the original department head, Wang Ziqian, was transferred to the Affairs Department. Wang began to organize and establish this department yesterday, and its functions are equivalent to those of the General Affairs and Port Affairs Bureau.

Establishment of the Nanshi Wharf Management Office 130

The case of the Nanshi steamship wharf being taken back and managed by the city has been in preparation for many years. The assets of the various ship companies and wharves have been priced and taken back, and the Port Affairs Bureau has been approved by the municipal government to establish the Nanshi Wharf Management Office to manage it. The office has already found a new building at the mouth of Maojia Lane on the Bund as its office location and has appointed Xu Shipu as the director. The office is divided into four sections: mooring, calculation, collection, and inspection. The various staff members have been separately appointed and officially established on July 1st, beginning to work. All shipping companies have paid sufficient deposits for renting wharf warehouses and bases and have signed contracts separately so that each ship can berth when it arrives at the port. The establishment of the management office is of great importance to the future national sovereignty and economy. It is hoped that it will be thoroughly reorganized so that our country's shipping industry will flourish day by day.

Local News Two

Student's New Work in the Longhai War 131

Comparable to British Students during the European War 132

During the European War, the youth of the various schools in the British Province of Qubate gathered students from all over the country to sew clothes and bandages for wounded soldiers and to perform all kinds of consolation duties. Other countries followed suit, and after the armistice, all countries admired the bravery of these youths, so they organized youth departments under the various national Red Cross Societies. More than 40 countries successively initiated and joined, undertaking the exchange of knowledge, communication of emotions, and development of industry and sanitation among the youth of the world to cultivate their nature of universal love and mutual assistance. The Chinese Red Cross Society also passed this case at its third conference, but unfortunately it was suspended due to a brawl and a forcible re-election. Unexpectedly, during this rescue operation in the Longhai War, the students of the Xinmin Society of Liukouji, Shangqiu County, organized a burial team of 30 people, who volunteered to be commanded by the rescue team of the Chinese Red Cross Society and were responsible for the burial work without taking any money, digging pits, burying bones, and clearing grass to find corpses. The Red Cross Society provided them with food to show preferential treatment. After receiving the report, Chairman Wang Peiyuan plans to submit it to the Standing Committee for commendation within the next few days. This can be compared to the students of England in the East and West during the European War.

Zhang Taijie Case Verdict 133

Zhang sentenced to three years of imprisonment

Lawyer Dong Yu declared not guilty

The case of Zhang Taijie, the general manager of the Sichuan-Lu Company, embezzling huge sums of road funds, involved lawyer Dong Yu. The District Court examined and debated the case together. Yesterday was the date of the verdict. At 12:00 noon, the verdict was announced in the first courtroom. The presiding judge was Shen Bingrong, the head of the Criminal Division, and the associate judges were Wu Zhen and Qian Chengjun. Prosecutor Yang Wenjun and clerk Yu Bi were present. After Zhang Taijie was brought in, Dong Yu also reported to the court. The trial judge first asked Zhang Taijie and Dong Yu for their age and place of origin. Zhang Taijie replied that he was 71 years old and from Sichuan. Dong Yu replied that he was 38 years old and from Wujin. The presiding judge stood up and read the verdict. Zhang Taijie was sentenced to three years of imprisonment for embezzlement in public office. The number of days of detention before the judgment was determined would be offset against the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Dong Yu was declared not guilty. After the verdict was announced, he said to Zhang Taijie that the part about Dong Yu was what you sued, but repeated examinations showed that there was no evidence and the suspicion was insufficient, so he was declared not guilty. You can appeal the part of your own sentence within ten days after receiving the judgment. Zhang replied that he certainly disagreed. The presiding judge then ordered Zhang Taijie to be returned to custody and Dong Yu to be handed over to his original guarantor. Then the court adjourned.

New Buildings on Mogan Mountain 134

A gospel for those seeking refuge from the summer heat Mogan Mountain in Wukang, Zhejiang Province, is a famous summer resort in the southeast. Every summer, Chinese and foreigners come here in droves. Since the Zhejiang Provincial Government established a special bureau to manage mountain affairs, the atmosphere has been completely new, and travelers have praised it. This year, the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction has made comprehensive plans to carry out four parts, and the funds are not taken from tourists at all, but completely from local construction funds. Since the start of construction, it has been actively carried out, and the following have been completed: (1) In terms of transportation, in addition to the completion of wireless and long-distance telephone installations, roads have also been opened up, road names have been designated, road signs have been erected, and the construction of bridges and wharves has been planned. (2) Regarding hygiene, water pools have been excavated, swimming pools have been established, sports facilities have been added, street lights, trash cans, and public toilets have been added, and hospitals and cemeteries have been planned. (3) Regarding construction, an electric power company, a meteorological station, and a nursery have been established, the Tushan Park has been renovated, and a public canteen, entertainment venues, and a Sun Yat-sen memorial tower have been built. (4) Regarding management, the management area has been determined and property taxes have been set up, all of which are being carried out in order. The mountain management authorities, seeing the presence of robbers from all directions, have also presented a petition to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to order a large security team to be stationed on the mountain to maintain law and order.

Auto Liquidation of the Pacific Trading Company 139

The Shanghai Branch Will Continue to Operate as Usual

The Da Wan Bao reported that the Pacific Trading Company, one of the oldest foreign firms established in China by the British, had convened a special meeting of shareholders on the 27th of last month by the London head office and decided to liquidate automatically. Director Creek was elected as the liquidator. The company's business has always been good. Even during the unfavorable cotton cloth market in Shanghai last year, it was still able to make a slight profit. This liquidation was due to the fact that two major shareholders had no intention of doing business in China. Today (the 1st), the company officially stated that the Shanghai branch will continue to operate as usual during the liquidation period, and before a satisfactory agreement is reached on whether the company will continue to maintain all or part of its business, the directors in Shanghai will temporarily preside over the liquidation affairs. It is now expected that the company may be reorganized. However, its employees in Shanghai are not willing to comment on this point today. It is also reported that the company has been established in Shanghai for nearly 80 years, and the name of the company in Western languages has been changed four times. The building at 21 Renji Road is its own property.

New Japanese-built Large Merchant Ship

The Japanese Mail Ship Company's newly built four excellent large ocean liners, of which the Terukuni Maru and the Hikawa Maru will arrive in Shanghai this month and sail to Europe. The Terukuni Maru has been introduced before, and the Hikawa Maru is scheduled to depart from Yokohama today (the 2nd) and stop at Kobe and Moji. It will take eight days to reach Shanghai, and it will sail to Hong Kong the next day. The details are as follows: Gross tonnage 11,600 tons, length 536 feet, width 66 feet, depth 41 feet, horsepower speed 18 knots, cabins first class 79 people, second class 69 people, third class 138 people. Construction started in 1928, launched in 1929, and completed in April of this year. It is indeed one of the world's leading ocean-going merchant ships.

Shanghai Weekly Forum Published 143

Seeking Trial Readers

In addition to daily newspapers, advanced countries in the East and West also have weekly newspapers that organize and systematize the news of a week and publish it in a collection so that the trends of contemporary politics and economics will be permanently preserved as historical records. The intention is excellent. In the United Kingdom, there are the Manchester Guardian Weekly and the London Weekly Mail, which have circulations of more than hundreds of thousands and are world-renowned weekly newspapers. Although China's news industry has gradually made progress in recent years, there is still a lack of news weeklies. Now, several like-minded people engaged in the news business have founded the Shanghai Weekly Forum, which will systematically compile the news of each week so that readers can have a clear understanding of the news and the development of the current situation in a week. In addition, there will be illustrated sections with photos, pictures, literature, and interesting works so that readers can increase their interests in many aspects after paying attention to the development of current affairs. The Shanghai Weekly Forum has now been published to the fourth issue, and the content and compilation are both excellent. In addition, the Shanghai Weekly Forum, in order to arouse students' attention to the current situation, is taking advantage of this summer vacation to solicit trial readers so that students can understand the development of the current situation at a very low cost. From July 1st, you only need to send a subscription fee of five jiao dollars to read the newspaper for two months (that is, eight issues), including postage. The company's address is at 8 Nanxin Kang Houses, Sichuan Road, Nanjing Road, Shanghai. Russian Automobile.

Lebad, the runner-up in France last year, is his top student. He has used a special machine bicycle to reach a speed of 130 kilometers per hour. Regulations of the Municipal Land Bureau.

Standards for Public and Private Riverbanks, Roads, and Alleys 159

The Municipal Land Bureau believes that the riverbanks, roads, and alleys in the city are complex and intertwined, and it is difficult to distinguish between public and private ownership, which hinders surveying and measurement. Therefore, it has specially formulated standards for public and private riverbanks, roads, and alleys, which are divided into three categories, and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval and announcement. The standards for public and private riverbanks, roads, and alleys in Shanghai are as follows: (1) Public and private riverbanks (a) Riverbanks with a length of more than 500 meters are considered public riverbanks, regardless of whether the riparian owners' deeds record any encroachment on the riverbank. (b) Riverbanks with a length of less than 500 meters are considered private riverbanks if the riparian owners have solid evidence to prove that they are privately owned. However, the land deeds of the riparian owners should still be reviewed to determine whether the area of the land exceeds the area recorded in the deed. Land exceeding the area recorded in the deed should be returned to the public. However, if the riverbank is necessary for irrigation of farmland, it cannot be arbitrarily blocked even if it is privately owned. The Land Bureau should indicate this on the land map. When the riverbank is no longer needed for irrigation in the future, the owner can apply for approval to return it to private farmland. (3) Public and private roads (a) Roads with a width of more than one meter and a length of more than 500 meters are considered public roads, regardless of whether the riparian owners' deeds record any encroachment on the road. (b) Roads with a width of less than one meter and a length of less than 500 meters are considered private roads if the riparian owners have solid evidence to prove that they are privately owned. However, the land deeds of the riparian owners should still be reviewed to determine whether the area of the land exceeds the area recorded in the deed. Land exceeding the area recorded in the deed should be returned to the public. However, if the road is an important thoroughfare for villages and towns, it cannot be arbitrarily blocked even if it is privately owned. The Land Bureau should indicate this on the land map. When the road is no longer needed for traffic in the future, the owner can apply for approval to return it to private use. (3) Public and private alleys Public alleys refer to alleys used by two or more owners. Public alleys used by two owners should be delineated on the land map, but it should be noted that they are for public use and cannot be blocked. Public alleys used by three or more owners should be specially indicated on the land map, but it should be noted that the property rights belong to each household, for example, a certain household has a share of a certain percentage of the total area of the alley and pays taxes according to the share. If three or more households unanimously agree to consider the alley as public land and are unwilling to pay taxes, the tax amount should be removed. On the land map, only the words "public alley" should be noted. If there are changes in property rights in the future, such as the gradual merger of property rights of each owner into one household, the household that merges the property can apply for approval from the Municipal Government to pay the taxes.

Public Utilities Bureau's Letter to Tenants of Yuqing Lane 160

Public Utilities Bureau's Letter to Tenants of Yuqing Lane, Zhabei: To the Residents of Yuqing Lane: "Houses in the Chinese Area Should Not Use Water and Electricity from the Concession." The houses in Yuqing Lane are entirely located in the Chinese area and are assigned by the competent authorities to the business area of the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company. From the perspective of national sovereignty and the authority of government agencies, there is no doubt that they should use water and electricity from the Chinese area. The Electricity Bureau has earnestly negotiated, and all households in the lane are supplied with electricity by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, which collects it from the Shanghai Power Company. The water supply should be handled in the same way. Therefore, this Bureau is doing its best to urge the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to connect the water pipes to Changchun Road for easy access to tap water in the Chinese area. Unexpectedly, the owners are pro-foreign and have repeatedly delayed the process, resulting in no progress. Everyone should know that using water and electricity from the concession not only damages sovereignty but also requires the payment of exorbitant taxes to the concession. If they resist, they will use vicious means such as power and water outages to restrain them. In 1927, the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession cut off the electricity to the lane and forced the collection of police taxes, which is a solid proof. I think the old tenants have not forgotten it. "Reasons Why the Public Utilities Bureau Prevented Foreign Merchants from Stopping Water and Cutting Off Pipes to Install Meters." On March 10, 1930, the Shanghai Water Company requested permission to move the water meters on one side of Changchun Road to the intersection of North Fourth, intending to escape the police authority of China and fulfill its selfish plan of permanent occupation. This Bureau immediately rejected it. Subsequently, the company arbitrarily cut off pipes to install meters, but was prevented by police officers from the Public Security Bureau. Unexpectedly, on the 28th of last month, the Public Works Bureau, without the permission of the Municipal Government, relied on a notice and actually cut off pipes to install meters on the sidewalk of North Sichuan Road on the morning of the 30th. This illegal act cannot be recognized. Therefore, we had to take decisive action. Yesterday, together with the Public Security and Public Works Bureaus, we sent personnel to cut off the water pipes in the lane. On the one hand, considering the need for water during the summer, we instructed the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to open the Taiping tap on Changchun Road and connect the water pipes in the lane to the water pipes in the Chinese area of Changchun Road to continue the water supply. I think the tenants can understand these intentions. "All Tenants Should Act Quickly to Solve the Water Supply Problem Together." Now it has been discovered that the water pipes connected in the lane are small pipes with a diameter of two inches, leading to Qixiu Lane, while the main pipe entering the lane from North Sichuan Road has a diameter of four inches, resulting in slightly weaker water pressure and inconvenience for residents living further away. This is because there was no time to choose carefully at the time of the emergency. This Bureau has now notified the owner to formally request water from the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company in order to connect the four-inch diameter main pipe. Therefore, please bear with it for the time being. If you really feel inconvenienced, you may urge the owner to follow the instructions of this Bureau to handle this matter. This matter is related to the vital interests of all tenants, and it is especially important during this hot summer season when the demand for water is high. We sincerely hope that you will act quickly and work together to solve it quickly and satisfactorily.

American-Asia Labor Dispute Resolved 161

Both Parties Signed Today; Full Resumption of Work Tomorrow. Since the strike by all workers of the American-Asia Silk Weaving Factory, located at 830 Avenue Petain, French Concession, along with its seven branches, on June 8, it has been almost a month. It is now known that yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau sent Wang Bing and the labor-management sides fully reconciled and settled the matter. This morning at 10:00 AM, both parties signed an agreement for full resumption of work tomorrow. As for the settlement terms, both parties agreed to restore the four terms of 1927, return the savings (to be returned on the 5th of this month), and pay severance pay to the three representatives who were fired, Lu, Zhang, and Wei. Thus, the labor dispute came to an end.

French Water and Electricity Labor Dispute Heard Yesterday 162

The labor dispute at the French Water and Electricity Company's engine room has been going on for half a month. Both sides have gone to extremes and have no hope of rapprochement. The following is an exploration of the situation yesterday: Warning to All Workers: The company posted a notice the day before yesterday stating that it would recruit new workers yesterday. The general workers were extremely angry, and the workers' representatives specially convened a temporary meeting yesterday afternoon to warn the workers to strictly abide by discipline, so there was no outrageous action. However, the new workers did not understand the content at first, so there were more than 20 people who were hired. The new workers said that they did not know the details. Only eight or nine people went to work in the afternoon, and the rest all dispersed. Some workers who dispersed took copper parts with them when they left the factory because they had not received wages for working for half a day. Two Notices from the Rice Association 163

Two Notices from the Rice Association Reorganization Committee (1) Notice Regarding the matter of informing: This association was ordered by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to handle the assessment of rice industry. The rice delivered will be evenly distributed according to the quantity to the registered rice shops who are required to pay and receive the rice. Although most people comply with the payment and rice collection, there are occasional cases of refusal to receive the rice due to slight discrepancies in the rice sample or slight changes in the rice quality. This shows a lack of understanding of the times. You should know that the evaluation of rice is actually the result of our shops suffering from the pain of cheap dark market prices. The Social Affairs Bureau is considerate of all parties and takes care of the people's food and carefully coordinates the emergency measures for the evaluation of rice. Our colleagues should understand the good intentions of the authorities and sacrifice a little. Since you have registered in advance, you should pay and receive the rice according to the assigned quantity. If there is a slight change or rottenness in the rice quality, you may screen it out and remove the bad ones. After this procedure, the quantity should be reported to this association for compensation. It is counterproductive to refuse to accept it because of this, and it will be even more difficult to do things in the future. May I ask what else can be done after this? Therefore, it is hereby notified that all registered rice shops that have not received the rice should pay and receive the allocated rice within two days. If you do not come to receive the rice after this deadline, your previous registration will be cancelled. This association will no longer accept any requests for rice in the future. Please pay attention to this. (2) To whom it may concern: Recently, due to the soaring price of rice and the posting of low prices in the dark market, rice shops have suffered greatly. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has instructed various rice industry organizations to organize an Evaluation Committee to unload the rice stored on ships under the Zhabei River. The Rice will be evenly distributed by this association. In addition to notifying the handling of the situation in advance, this association will hold a general membership meeting at 2:00 PM on July 3 at the Jiagutang Guild Hall in Danfenglou, Danfeng Street. Please all members attend on time to discuss the progress of the evaluation of rice. This matter concerns the vital interests of our colleagues. Please attend on time and do not give up this opportunity.

Central Bank Inspection Report 164

The 58th Central Bank Issuance Reserve Inspection Report: This committee, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Act, is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the banknotes issued by the bank. Now, on June 30th of the 19th year of the Republic of China, the 58th inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this bank, and the inspection results are hereby announced as follows: Total amount of banknotes issued: Silver dollars 16,700,785. Within this amount: Silver dollar notes 15,579,063 yuan, fractional currency notes 12 totaling silver dollars 1,128,791 yuan. Total amount of banknote reserves: 16,700,785 silver dollars. Within this amount: Cash reserve silver dollars 13,818,355.60. This cash reserve is stored as follows: 10,815,006.73 yuan in the bank's issuing vault, 1,211,635.14 yuan in branches in various ports, and 1,791,713.73 yuan in other banks. Guarantee reserve equivalent to 2,889,498.40 silver dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve should be 60% and the guarantee reserve should be 40%. The inspection results showed that the cash exceeded 60% and the guarantee was less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is made on June 30th of the 19th year of the Republic of China. Chairman of the Supervisory Board of the Central Bank: Li Fusun, Supervisors: Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilong.

Yesterday's Plenary Executive Committee Meeting 167

Reporting on the Petition to Nanjing. The Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Industry, suffering from economic invasion and various inescapable circumstances, specially dispatched representatives to Nanjing to petition for relief, as reported previously. It is now learned that the representatives returned to Shanghai together on the 28th. Fellow industrialists flocked to the station to welcome them and inquire about the situation. It is said that the outcome is quite promising. Yesterday, a plenary executive committee meeting was convened. After the ceremony, Chairman Wu Tingsheng reported on the purpose of the meeting, saying that the delegation to Nanjing, entrusted by fellow industrialists to petition the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and the Ministry of Finance, was unprecedented in the history of the association and was truly a last resort in the cigarette industry. The exchange rate of gold has never been so high, even doubling compared to the previous year, and although the tax rates were set at the time of the unified tax, the order restricting the sale price was only issued last October. If the government had known about the huge fluctuations in the gold exchange rate at that time, it would not have disregarded the life and death of the Chinese cigarette industry. Now that our fellow industrialists are at the end of their rope, we have no time to lose and have prepared three measures to petition the government to rescue the remaining cigarette factories and consider the livelihoods of tens of thousands of workers. We were unanimously approved by the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The main points of the assistance were seen in the previous report. Finally, we presented the situation to the Ministry of Finance, hoping to obtain practical relief measures. Secretary Li Yunong received us and conducted a detailed investigation into the various difficulties of the cigarette factories regarding raw materials, foreign exchange, taxes, and price limits, as well as the closure of nearly twenty large and small cigarette factories, proving that the manufacturers' capabilities were exhausted and that immediate relief was necessary. Secretary Wang expressed understanding and was concerned about economic invasion. He inquired about the flower purchasing situation of Chinese and foreign cigarette merchants. We replied that Chinese merchants had weak capital and could only buy in small quantities, making it difficult to gain the trust of the authorities. Secretary Li promised to actively seek ways to alleviate the hidden pain of Chinese merchants. We felt satisfied and returned to Shanghai. The petition mission can be considered complete. All our fellow industrialists must continue to work hard. Next, Economic Standing Committee member Shen Liangde reported on the income and expenditure and uses of the petition. Next, resolutions were made on matters related to the follow-up of the petition: (1) If this petition does not have a satisfactory effect, what should be done? It was resolved that at this critical juncture, a more advanced petition must be made. (2) It was recommended that Xia Juchuan, Dai Gengxin, and Lao Jingxiu negotiate with important figures in the banking industry in this city (omitted below). The resolution was passed. (3) The party and government organs in this city have made efforts after accepting the petition of this association. How should we express our gratitude? It was resolved to respectfully express our gratitude and request continued promotion, and Yu Yuqin, Li Xuedong, Wang Qiuquan, Jiang Pinyu, and Bao Gengsheng were appointed to take charge. (4) Inquire about how the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce is expressing its support for the petition of this association. It was resolved to send Shen Liangde and Lao Jingxiu to inquire. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Jisheng Society Asks for Relief for Jinsuo Town 168

The Chinese Jisheng Society recently received reports from Zhang Pengzhu, Magistrate of Siyang County, Jiangsu Province; Chen Jianzheng, Mayor of Jinsuo Town; Chen Tingju, District Chief of the Third District; Zhou Yuankai, President of the Qingjiang Branch of the Chinese Jisheng Society; and Li Xilin, Vice President of the same, stating that the town of Siyang is located in a strategic, densely populated, and low-lying area, and its people suffer from poverty. The third district in the west of Siyang is the worst. The third district borders Hongze Lake and is connected to Si County, Anhui Province and Suqian County, Jiangsu Province. Banditry is rampant. The Jinsuo Town relies on it as a barrier, and the people are living in peace. Jinsuo Town is a commercial hub with dense population, and it is an important town in the west of Siyang and a security for Anhui-Si and Su-Si-Suqian counties. Last winter, bandits such as Wei Yisan first occupied Lujiawei in Siyang, and then occupied the villages along the border of the Siyang-Suqian-Si counties such as Tujia Garden, Suqian Zhatang Town. Although they have been harmed, Jinsuo Town has stood still, and the bandits have not dared to break through. On April 20th of this year, bandits Wei Yisan suddenly led a party of thousands of people to surround and attack the town. Liu Bingquan, an instructor of the town's security group, supervised the group members and the public to resist to the death. After two days and nights of fierce fighting, the county chief of Siyang and the county chief of Suqian each led the public security team of Siyang and Suqian counties and the public security team of Su-Su-Shu counties to rush to support them. However, the town was finally captured by the bandits, killing more than 300 men and women, injuring and kidnapping more than the number of deaths. More than half of the houses were burned, more than 700 households and thousands of houses, and the entire town was looted. No household was spared. The corpses piled up like mountains, and blood flowed like rivers. The town became an unprecedented disaster. People were steamed in pots and used to feed pigs. People were cut into pieces with knives and cooked. It was better to be bombed to death with guns and leave bones. The whole town was smelly and steamed for miles. The disaster was more fierce than floods and beasts. The military, police and compatriots saw it together. Since the fall of Jinsuo Town, the fortress of Siyang, Siyang and Suqian counties has been lost, and bandits have been rampant and ravaging an area nearly 100 miles wide. The soldiers came and the bandits went, and the disaster was unprecedented. Now, the dead in the town have no coffins to bury, the injured have no medicine to heal, the kidnapped have no strength to rescue, and the burned have no houses to live in. We have seen the hearts of the people are hurt, and the relief is inadequate. Dare to imitate the cry of the Qin Court and the call of the uncle, ask for the transfer of relief funds to help the orphans and widows. I can't bear to urgently lead and wait for orders. The association should take the disaster situation in the town as urgent and the relief should be expedited. However, the strength is too weak to win the rescue, and it has been requested to jointly organize the Jiangsu Yizhen Association to rescue the dying disaster victims in case of one. Such natural disasters and bandit disasters are becoming more and more intense, and the rescue is not enough. It is truly an unprecedented catastrophe.

Fire in the French Concession 170

Fire at Deyuanxiang Shoe Store - Heavy losses. At around 1:00 AM this morning, a fire broke out at Xinxinqiao intersection on Dama Road in the French Concession. The fire spread and was gradually extinguished at 2:30 AM this morning. The reporter of this newspaper went to the scene to investigate and found that the fire started on the upper floor of the Deyuanxiang Shoe Store. Deyuanxiang Shoe Store is a double-fronted store with house numbers 545 and 543. The boss, Zhu Fengshan, is from Wuxi, is in his 40s, and has more than a dozen employees. The upper floor is rented to the Far East Hotel for business. At around 1:00 AM this morning, the fire suddenly broke out on the upper floor. Everyone was asleep in the middle of the night and was awakened in shock. Fortunately, no one was injured. The facade of Wantai Leg Restaurant at No. 541 on the east side was also affected, and the Tengfang Tea Food Store on the west side suffered minor losses. Deyuanxiang Shoe Store was originally located at the intersection of Gongguan Road, Dongxinqiao. Due to the renovation of the building, it moved to its current location on the 18th of last month. It has not been open for long when it suddenly suffered a fire. All the goods were burned, which is also very unfortunate. The boss, Zhu, fled in fear of crime when the fire broke out. He was captured by the French Concession police detectives, and some employees are being closely investigated.

Letter from the Western Paint Association to Fellow Industrialists to Merge into the Association 173

The Shanghai Special Municipal Western Paint Industry Association has been formally established. All former paint industry members affiliated with the Shanghai Foreign Goods Commercial Association are no longer a legal organization. The association sent a letter to the paint industry members yesterday, stating that the association was established under the guidance of the relevant authorities in accordance with the Industrial and Commercial Association Law and the Industrial and Commercial Association Organization Procedures promulgated by Instruction No. 734 of the National Government. The association stated that the members of the paint industry affiliated with the association, such as Gonghe and more than a dozen others, had a narrow organizational view based on free will at the time. It seems that they were temporarily waiting for the transfer of appropriate organizations. Although the organization is not based on laws and regulations and party guidance, the purpose, foundation, and ties to the association, the correction of business operations, and the maintenance and promotion of the common interests of the industry must be the same. The association has been formally established and should be integrated into the association in accordance with the law to create a unified whole, merge water and milk, gather healthy and complete unity, and jointly plan for the welfare of the industry and the advancement of the future. The association believes that the paint industry members in the association must also have this kind of expectation, and anyone with a little knowledge will not have a contrary opinion. On the 17th of this month, the association held a general meeting to elect the first executive committee and had previously sent a letter urging the submission of a member list to re-elect the government. However, the association has not replied, giving up its voting rights, which is regrettable. In order to implement Article 5 of the Industrial and Commercial Association Law, the association sincerely and earnestly makes a final recommendation in this spirit. It is hoped that the association will compile a list of all the affiliated paint industry members and transfer them to the association in order to comply with laws and regulations and strengthen the system. The association hopes to hear back from the association.

Laugh It Off Haike 177

Philosopher: A person should be optimistic about everything and should not be pessimistic and suffer. If troubles come, they should try to avoid them. Optimist: Yes, so when creditors write to me to demand payment, I always burn them and don't take them to heart. A: How can your son swim at such a young age? Where did he learn it? B: In the bathtub. Old gentleman: You young people must not be afraid of difficulties and must take on everything and bear heavy responsibilities. Young man: What the old gentleman said is absolutely right, so every day when I go back from the office, I have to carry my newlywed wife from downstairs to upstairs. Isn't this the way to bear heavy responsibilities and go far? A: I saw a beautiful young man sitting in a car with you yesterday, but it seemed like he only had one arm. B: He has two arms, but one arm is hidden around my waist. A: Sister C is learning to sing. Her throat is suitable for low notes. Why does she have to sing high notes? B: Prepare to fight with her husband after she gets married so that she can shake the house with her voice and subdue him.

A Record of the China Youth Asia Walking Group 178

Departure Zhao Dingming At 10:00 am on June 28th, 19th year of the Republic of China, the China Youth Asia Walking Group departed from the North Railway Station in Shanghai, the national cultural center. Before the departure, I was able to participate in the farewell in my busy schedule. I can't express the joy in my heart. When I arrived at the railway station, I saw men and women coming and going on the platform. The most striking things were the flags of the Yousheng Travel Group and the flags presented to the Asian Walking Group by the Camel Travel Team Yuehua Orchestra. Mr. Huang Jingwan vigorously presented the group with "Cherish the reputation of the group, respect public resolutions, visit and take notes everywhere, be considerate of the physical and mental health of female friends, get enough sleep at night, pay attention to cold and heat, pay attention to the suffering of the people, maintain the peace of the whole body, awaken the patriotism of overseas Chinese, and often send good news to the Shanghai newspaper." Photographers such as Guo Xiqilin, Xu Jinzhi, and Shao Woyun competed to take pictures. Speaking of the members of each group, they all wore white copper basin hats, yellow cloth boy scout uniforms, yellow leg bands, and black leather shoes, which were very neat and energetic in appearance. At this time, it was only 9:00 clock. The female members of the group, Hu Sujuan and Cui Xiaogiong, were very calm and paced back and forth. Qiu Fang was very interested and the photographers took pictures of her beautiful figure one after another. At 10:00 am, the photographers officially took several group photos of them on the railway platform and took several photos with the relatives and friends who were seeing them off. Then came Mr. Huang Jingwan's message and the reply from Huang Yue, the group's social worker. The general idea of the reply was that they had been preparing for a long time and were finally able to set off today. They were striving for the glory of our nation and promoting the spirit of youth adventure, as well as the plan to investigate the lives of our nation, which began to be implemented today. They would infuse this matter with a spirit of perseverance and all their strength, and their footprints would travel all over Asia. After speaking, they asked the stationmaster and the chief of transportation to sign to confirm the group before they departed in an orderly manner along the railway track. Everyone shouted "Long live the Chinese nation" and "Success to the walking group" and set off the firecrackers bought by Mr. Huang. For a time, the crackling sound and the enthusiastic atmosphere of representatives from various schools and agencies raising their hats and waving handkerchiefs were tense at the station.

Travel Notes of Hong Kong and Macao (Part 2) Yin Zibai 179

After a week of touring Hong Kong, I took the Chinese steamer Quanzhou to Macau. The voyage was extremely fast, departing at 2:00 pm and arriving at 5:30 pm. I stayed at the President Hotel, which had halls named after Sun Yat-sen, Yuan Shikai, Huang Xing, and Feng Guozhang. The streets in the city were called New Road and Seashore Road. Apart from smoking, gambling, and prostitution, there was no legitimate business in the city. Those who could be called industrialists were the electrical plant, salt, and fishing companies. There were more than 700 fishing boats on the coast, and each time they went to sea, they had to store enough salt because the salt particles in Annam were too large and not suitable for pickling fish. It was necessary to crush the salt by hand, which was clumsy and laborious. The Yu Wuhe Refined Salt Company had a self-made crushing machine and should allow me to donate one to my friend in order to increase the production rate. However, Mr. Zheng still earnestly consulted me about the sales of domestic salt. The patriotism of the overseas Chinese is truly admirable. Macau was originally a corner of Zhongshan County and was leased to Portugal. Surprisingly, it built fortresses and moored three warships in the sea, which were small and old. It had a governor and various judicial and administrative halls. The total number of officials, including the national shipyard, barracks, and ship captains, was no less than thirty or forty, which was more than the merchants in the country. There were car companies that could reach Qiguan in Zhongshan County. There were various gambling casinos, including Shampiao shops, Piao Baige Piao, and Baoju. They were also called companies and numbered more than ten. The annual gambling tax was more than one million. Opium was established with a special sales bureau. There were two or thirty brothels. The opium dens were called talking rooms. There were five cinemas showing domestic films. When Che Chi was released, the seats were full. The schools were still lecturing on scriptures, and there were even more private schools. There were Confucius respect associations and Confucius education associations, and the Confucius birthday was exceptionally lively. Even shops had to hang lights to celebrate. Kowloon was a leased territory of Hong Kong, and the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Station was located there. Public buses were used for transportation in the city to Kowloon City, Yau Ma Tei, Tsim Sha Tsui, Mong Kok, Yang Shui Po, Lai Chi Kok, To Kwa Wan, Tai Wan, etc. The largest hotel was the Peninsula Hotel, which cost 1.5 million gold to build. There were also seven or eight cinemas, about half of which showed domestic films. There were six ferries between Kowloon and Hong Kong, which departed as soon as they arrived and had good order. The fare for first class was one dime and the fare for third class was five cents. Hong Kong Island was narrow and densely populated, and the rent for housing was surprisingly high (one and a half times higher than Shanghai). Therefore, Kowloon has become a factory and residential area. The gold was expensive and the silver was cheap, not only was the domestic panic, but the panic of using silver in Hong Kong was the same. The Hong Kong government held meetings for several days, convening non-official members to discuss the matter repeatedly. According to the British merchants' proposal, the government changed to the imaginary gold standard. The Chinese merchants believed that Hong Kong's trade should still use silver currency because China's standard used silver. Finally, it was resolved to prohibit the import of Mexican silver dollars and only allow each person to carry fifty yuan in order to avoid the flooding of silver coins in the market. In addition, public officials were affected by the decline in silver and it was resolved to increase their living expenses by 20%. This increase in expenses would be compensated for by increasing taxes on tobacco and alcohol.

Tan Yi in Jinghua is Solemn 180

Benli promotes the art of Go. News from the Shanghai-Hankou Go community has already been recorded. What about Beijing? It is also worth recording. People in Beijing like to gamble, but Go is not strong in general society. In the entire city, there is no formal research organization. Only two teahouses near the Confucius Temple have set aside some seats to serve as Go markets. The situation is similar to that of the Zhongxin Building in Shanghai, but the seat is dirty and noisy, even worse than the Zhongxin Building. One teahouse is called Shiyinyuan and the other is called Wencai Teahouse. Quite a few people rely on it to make a living. People in Beijing generally call them Go Hun. Occasionally, one or two connoisseurs go to watch, and these people will try their best to play Go with them, slightly preparing small prizes to win a little money. The scene is very pitiful. A gentleman once initiated and raised funds to set up a Go club on the banks of the Qinhuai River, imitating the example of billiard rooms, with the players paying rent and carefully arranging the seating and furnishings to make it exquisite and spacious, so that the players could devote more effort to this art in a comfortable environment. Later, I don't know how this plan ended up failing, and the municipal authorities did not pay attention to it. The public tea garden run by the municipal government originally had a variety of Go and Chinese chess, but recently it has gradually decreased and only one set of Go remains for guests. There is also a Chinese chess market in the old Pan Palace of the Confucius Temple, which is even more crude. In addition, there is also a Chinese chess market nearby.

Pomona College Awards Mei Lanfang Honorary Doctorate - Excerpts (Continued) 181

When the tour concludes, I trust that everyone's understanding and sympathy towards our nation will deepen. This isn't just about our artistic success, but also about the kindness of your people in understanding the purpose of our tour. In a broader sense, our visit is to contribute our small efforts to the progress of civilized humanity. My most sincere hope for peace, as historically proven, cannot be achieved through military might. The peace that humanity desires isn't merely the calm after a storm. True peace comes from enhancing human development and growth in spirit, intellect, and material well-being. To maintain genuine world peace, humanity must understand, forgive, and sympathize with each other, supporting each other rather than engaging in conflict. The peace that our two great nations, China and America, hope for is based on international trust and goodwill. To achieve this goal, everyone needs concrete research in the arts and sciences, understanding each other's customs, historical backgrounds, problems, and difficulties. I, Lanfang, came here to study the dramatic arts of your country and have benefited greatly from the kindness of your people. My performances of ancient Chinese dramatic art are far from perfect, and I am humbled by your praise. However, I know that your actions are not just an award for my personal skills, but an expression of sympathy for Chinese culture and friendship with the Chinese people. Only in this way dare I accept such great honor. In the future, I will work even harder to be worthy of being part of the Pomona College family, to live up to everyone's recognition." Mr. Mei Qiju then repeated this in English. After the speech, applause thundered for several minutes. Immediately, the American national anthem was played, and the students in academic gowns sang the anthem while standing. After the ceremony, all the doctors came to shake hands and offer congratulations. The president and other officials present said that Mr. Mei's speech was exceptionally profound and immediately requested the full text to be printed and distributed to the students for permanent preservation. Then, everyone took photos together, and another photo was taken with the president. Afterwards, the president specially invited Mr. Mei and the others to a dinner party with over thirty tables and more than ten people in the college dining hall. I, Mr. Mei, and our colleagues sat at two tables, with the president's family, Dr. Dengqin's family, and several professors. The remaining three hundred or so students were also present, sharing the meal to show intimacy. As the meal was about to end, students from the music group stood up and sang twice to show respect, and then moved to Mr. Mei's seat to sing, especially to express goodwill. After the meal, the president led a tour of the dormitories and other places. It was already eight o'clock, so we took our leave and returned. Mr. Mei, Dr. Xu Zhang, and I rode in the same car. Along the way, the flowers and trees were lush, especially the many citrus trees with buds full of branches, exceptionally beautiful. The next day, all the newspapers competed to report the story in detail.

There is a force that is more widespread than Weiqi (Go), but its lack of organization and research spirit is far inferior to Weiqi. I secretly believe that both Weiqi and Xiangqi (Chinese chess) are national Chinese games, but because those in authority do not know how to promote them, these great arts have been reduced to gambling tools. It is a pity. As the Beijing Municipal authorities have recently held many pinball and table tennis competitions, their purpose is nothing more than to promote noble entertainment for the public. I sincerely hope that the authorities can hold a Weiqi competition again in the near future.

European Travelogue (61) Liu Haisu 182

French Autumn Salon (3) My Journey of Submitting Works (Part 1) Haisu, your energy is admirable, and I often worry about you because you have too many and too heavy "non-artistic" responsibilities at home. Some with weaker constitutions might have been crushed long ago, but you are still so free and vigorous, which truly makes me happy. However, fatigue is ultimately not a tonic for artists. Haisu, you have the power, and you have already reached the shore of art. You must make up your mind, tighten your belt, and run deeper. There, you can find greater companions: Van Gogh, Titian, Cézanne.

This is a passage from a letter my friend Xu Zhimo sent me from Beijing on September 3, fifteen years ago. Zhimo was one of my most ardent supporters, and I was well aware of this, so I had been preparing to leave the country several times. Who would be willing to submit to the base and turbid ground, wasting limited time? In the spring of fifteen years, I decided to come to Europe, and all the procedures were prepared. Suddenly, like a bolt from the blue, Sun Chuanfang strictly prohibited "models," so I had to argue with him. He gained strength and intensified his oppression, but I could not give in to him. After arguing for a year, I was finally able to set sail across the sea the year before last.

After arriving in Europe, my first natural thought was to seek some knowledge for myself. I was determined to bury myself in hard work for a few years and decided not to care about anything else, focusing solely on painting. Second, because the trends of modern art were constantly changing and surging every day, but in this flow, the surging was always a fierce advance towards the world desired by the self. Recently, with France as the center, the world's artistic trends were establishing a unique spirit of modernity with the courage to negate everything and the ardent hope to establish the self. In this turbulent vortex, I also wanted to muster my courage, establish my ardent hope, and present my works to the artistic center of the world, Paris. Therefore, I planned to hold a solo exhibition in Paris next spring. Before holding a solo exhibition, I originally did not want to submit works to any exhibition.

In late September 1929, we returned to France from Geneva for the first time, passing by the Faculty of Arts Hotel across from the University of Paris. One morning, on a clear and bright day, I was on the third floor of the Faculty of Arts Hotel, looking down at the pedestrians on the street from the window when:

"Hey, Mr. Liu, the Autumn Salon is about to open!" Liu Kangjun walked in and shouted loudly.

"It's still early. It will have to wait another month or two," I said, calculating, and answered him lazily and frankly. Then, Chen Renhao and Fu Nu'an also walked in. Mr. Chen also looked like he was reporting a major event and said,

"This morning, we got a few copies of the submission regulations for the Autumn Salon from Academie Colarossi. We all want to submit works. We hope Mr. Liu will also submit works. Are you willing?"

I thought this was indeed a major event.

"Of course, I am willing to accompany you, but I want to hold a solo exhibition."

I thought and said this at the same time.

"The Autumn Salon is against the official Salon. It is a fresh and progressive Salon, very suitable for your spirit. Before you hold a solo exhibition, you might as well submit once," Mr. Fu also encouraged me in this way.

"That's fine. I'll just take an old work and try it out because my new works are all stored in the countryside, and it would be too troublesome to unpack them for a while. And I also want to use a pseudonym," I replied, meaning that I still did not want to casually submit new works to any Salon in the first place.

"Great, then let's go and select some works."

"We should send them in these few days. The deadline for submissions is September 30," Mr. Fu said, looking at the Salon's regulations.

Silver Loan Amount for June 184

The amount of silver loans traded each day in June varied greatly. The fluctuations were particularly intense, reaching a high of 6 cents and a low of only 4 cents, a difference of 15%, which can be described as a drastic change in the market. As such, the total daily amount of silver loans was higher than in the previous month. Fortunately, the second half of the month eased, so the total amount for the month was only 5 taels, 3 mace, 4 fen. Adding June 1, which was the Summer Solstice holiday, with 2 mace, the total would be 5 taels, 5 mace, 4 fen. The daily average would be 1 mace, 8 fen, 4 li, 6.7 hao. On Japan's Capital Export 189

Propose Moving Factories to China and India

Recent Aggression Policy

Due to various factors, Japanese cotton mills' exports are sluggish, and domestic demand is also sluggish, leading to a state of poverty. Reducing work, reducing capital, or reducing workers seems to be the only strategy for manufacturers. However, considering the example of Kanebo, they must be careful. Therefore, overseas development is an inevitable trend. According to Japanese newspapers, in this environment, the so-called "capital export theory" is gradually gaining attention in Japan. If our Chinese factories are oppressed by foreign factories in the future, it will be even worse than it is today. The translation of their remarks is as follows: In addition to maintaining the existing markets in India and China, it is indeed advisable for the Japanese textile industry to seek new ways to exploit resources in those two countries. To this end, it should be determined to export capital instead of products. In the current situation, moving the spindles remaining from the reduction of work in Japanese domestic factories to China should be the first step in the plan for China. However, considering the current situation in China, the degree of need is still too early. However, from a favorable perspective, the production cost in China, with its low labor costs, working hours, and taxes, is about half that of Japan. Although China is frequently in internal strife, transportation is inconvenient, people's livelihoods are haggard, and goods are blocked, these are temporary phenomena. If domestic stability increases the need, the current Japanese goods in China will not be enough to supply the needs. After the establishment of the Sino-Japanese tariff agreement, the current 75% ad valorem tax on yarn and cloth will not be affected. If the new national tariff regulations are implemented, the tariff on cotton textiles may be collected within a range of 125. The impact on the annual export of over 186 million yuan (last year's statistics) to China will be enormous. Therefore, investing in enterprises in China is the trend in the future. In addition to investing in China, India can also be invested in and operated in the same way. Because India is increasing tariffs, Japan is hit hard. If the policy is not changed, the export route will be blocked. Financial and textile companies are already conducting surveys. This kind of news is most worthy of our attention.

Food River Measurement Stopped Again 190

Zhabei

Yesterday, at the river, rice boats turned back from Huangdu on the fifth. It was reported that this batch had been delayed while watching the situation in Shanghai. Currently, there are more than 20 boats in the river. Because the rice shops delayed in collecting the rice, the appraisal bureau had advanced a large amount of money for the rice measurement in recent days. Therefore, it had to stop the measurement. Once the goods have been measured, the merchants must settle the account and take the money back to their villages. However, the rice shops, firstly, must bring the money when they go to the bureau to collect the white rice, so the smaller shops inevitably feel a little financial difficulty, and thus delay in collecting and transporting the rice (previously, the rice shops settled accounts at the end of each month, but now they are all paid in cash). Secondly, the rice measured by the appraisal bureau naturally varies in quality, so the shops inevitably choose. However, there is a distinction between those who collect first and those who collect later, and those who arrive later do not seem very satisfied. Therefore, they are watching again. However, the appraisal bureau's advances are limited, and once there is a delay, it is difficult to maintain, so it has to be temporarily suspended. The price of Yang Du Jian tends to soften due to the weakness of foreign rice, and both the arrival of goods and sales are sluggish. All transactions are rare.

Yesterday was the mid-year settlement day for the foreign firms in the city, and the customs closed as usual. Silk firms will also take a two-day holiday and will reopen as usual on the 3rd.

Jiashan Summer Silkworms Generally Unfavorable 195

Because farmers in the four rural villages of Jiaxing had a poor spring cocoon harvest this year, they all raised summer silkworms. The amount raised was not weak. However, the climate was bad. At first, it was extremely cold, then there were strong winds, thunder, and rain, and finally, it was hot and humid, so the silkworm larvae were greatly affected. Most of them were found to have died of stiffness. Currently, the early silkworms are already in the major sleeping stage to open their leaves, and the late gang is also about to enter the sleeping stage. The summer cocoon harvest this year will still be reduced.

Dantu New Summer Cocoons Poor Harvest 196

Totaling Up To Four-Tenths of the Harvest

Because the government and silk merchants promoted the raising of summer cocoons and issued silkworm eggs, the amount raised by farmers in the towns and villages of Dantu County this year was very smooth. Unfortunately, the weather was very cold and rainy at first, followed by hot and humid thunderstorms, causing the silkworm larvae to change before and after the major sleep. Although they tried to take care of them, 50% to 60% of them were lost to white stiffness and yellow discharge. The new cocoons have already been launched on the market. The total cocoon production in the four rural villages totaled four-tenths of the harvest. The age-old cocoon firms opened their scales yesterday. The initial price of cocoons was 50 to 55 yuan. The high-quality cocoons were priced as high as 60 yuan.
